  3. X or Y is H accompaniment by condition 3. Also, F and G do not share accompaniment by condition 4.This means X is either F or G accompanist. By condition 1, if X is F accompanist, then W is L accompanist, but G cannot have (W, Y) as accompanists. So, X must be G accompanist, and Y is either F or L accompanist. Now if Y is F accompanist, (D) is false. Otherwise, if Y is L accompanist, then Y cannot be H accompanist as X or Y is H accompanist and W is L accompanist. Hence (C) is also false. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 8:
Thought: We need to deduce which singers have Y as an accompanist and apply the given conditions to see if any of the pairs in the choices violate them. 
Action: We can know from conditions (2) and (3) that X cannot be H's accompaniment  and also that either X or Y has to be H's accompaniment. Also, X cannot be M's accompaniment. Thus, Y should be H and L's accompanist. Also, X will be F's and K's accompanist so Y cannot be their accompanist. From condition (4), we can see that L is not an accompanist of F or G, and M is not an accompanist of F or H. Therefore, Y cannot be an accompanist for F and M which is stated in choice (D). Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Thought:
  If Y is H accompaniment, then according to known condition (3), X is H accompaniment which is a contradiction because X and Y cannot share accompaniment.
  Therefore, from known condition (3), X should be H accompaniment which means that Y is either F or G accompaniment.
  From known condition (1), if X is F accompaniment, then W is L accompaniment.
  If Y is F accompaniment, according to known condition (2), X is G accompaniment which violates the known condition (4).
  Therefore, Y must be G accompaniment which means that W is K accompaniment and X is H accompaniment.
  So, Y cannot accompany L and H because they will share the same accompanimentist.
Action: Answer("B")

  The question requires finding the maximum number of chefs meeting the given conditions.
  If there are N chefs and each chef has 2 dishes, there would be a total of 2N dishes.
  No two people have the same dishes, so there would be a total of 2N dishes.
  There are 3 grades that can be assigned to each dish, so the total number of possible grade combinations is 3^(2N).
  Every pair of chefs can be compared to each other, so for each Chef A, there would be N-1 chefs to compare to. 
  
    If all N chefs are more skilled than Chef B, there would be no solution.
    If N-1 chefs are more skilled than Chef B, there would be only one chef that is not better than Chef B.
    If N-2 chefs are more skilled than Chef B, there would be two chefs that are not better than Chef B.
    The number of chefs that are not better than Chef B cannot be greater than two.
  
  Based on the above reasoning, let’s try to find the maximum value of N.
  
    For N = 1, there would be only one hot dish and one cold dish, so there would be only 9 possible combinations of 2 dishes. There are 3^2 possible grade combinations for each chef. Suppose Chef A has the highest grade for both dishes and Chef B has the lowest grade for both dishes. Since the question states that "at least one item is higher than Chef B", this condition is not met.
    
    For N = 2, there would be 4 hot dishes and 4 cold dishes, so there would be only 144 possible combinations of 4 dishes. There are 3^4 possible grade combinations for each chef. Let's assume that Chef A has the highest grades for all dishes and Chef B has the lowest grades for all dishes. Then, we can compare each Chef A’s dish grade to the corresponding Chef B’s grade. There must be at least one dish that Chef A has a higher grade than Chef B to meet the condition. Therefore, there can be at most 1 chef with at least one dish grade lower than Chef B's grades.
    
    For N = 3, there would be 6 hot dishes and 6 cold dishes, so there would be only 5,184 possible combinations of 6 dishes. There are 3^6 possible grade combinations for each chef. Let's assume that Chef A has the highest grades for all dishes and Chef B has the lowest grades for all dishes. We can compare each Chef A’s dish grade to Chef B’s dish grade to form 12 grade comparisons. Since there must be at least one dish with a higher grade than Chef B's grades, and the maximum number of chefs that are not better than Chef B cannot be greater than 2, there can be at most 2 chefs with at least one dish grade lower than Chef B's. 
  
  Therefore, the maximum number of chefs that can meet the above conditions is 3.

  C: Although there are many different explanations for the origin of the Gua name, it is inseparable from its sect, either attributed to the theory of fetching images, or attributed to the theory of fetching meanings

  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5

  From (2), we know I and E are adjacent i.e. I is either to north of E or south of E.
  If I is north of E then the arrangement becomes G I E F H which can be reversed to H F E I G
  If I is south of E then the arrangement becomes G E I F H which can be reversed to H F I E G
  So there are two possible arrangements.

  A: 2 rooms
  B: 3 rooms
  C: 4
  D: 5 rooms

  There are only 6 warehouses,
  one of which stores M, G, L, T, F, P.

    * G warehouse number is greater than L warehouse number, so G is in 4th, 5th or 6th warehouse.

    * P warehouse number is greater than F warehouse number, so P is in 2nd, 3rd, 4th, 5th or 6th warehouse.
